I found the issue! Looking at line 248-253, the `RelatedFieldListFilter.has_output()` method returns `True` if there are enough choices (considering the empty choice if applicable). However, the logic seems to be checking:\n\n```python\nreturn len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 1\n```\n\nWhere `extra` is 1 if `include_empty_choice` is True, or 0 otherwise.\n\nThis means:\n- If lookup_choices is empty (0 items) and include_empty_choice is False (extra=0): returns 0 + 0 > 1 = False ✓ (correct)\n- If lookup_choices is empty (0 items) and include_empty_choice is True (extra=1): returns 0 + 1 > 1 = False ✓ (correct)\n- If lookup_choices has 1 item and include_empty_choice is False (extra=0): returns 1 + 0 > 1 = False (this is the issue!)\n- If lookup_choices has 1 item and include_empty_choice is True (extra=1): returns 1 + 1 > 1 = True ✓\n\nActually wait, let me reread this. The method is checking if `len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 1`. This is meant to hide the filter if there's only 1 choice total (including the \"All\" option which is always shown).\n\nBut the problem is:\n- The \"All\" option is always shown (see line 291-297 in the choices method)\n- If there are no lookup_choices and no include_empty_choice, then the only option is \"All\", and the filter should be hidden\n- If there are lookup_choices and include_empty_choice, the options are: \"All\", the choices, and the empty option\n\nSo the logic should be:\n- If lookup_choices is empty and not include_empty_choice: return False (only \"All\" option)\n\n\n- Otherwise: return True\n\nBut currently the logic checks if `len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 1`. Let me trace through the cases:\n- 0 + 0 > 1 = False ✓ (correct for no choices case)\n- 0 + 1 > 1 = False ✓ (correct for empty choice only case)\n- 1 + 0 > 1 = False ✗ (should be True if there's 1 choice)\n- 1 + 1 > 1 = True ✓ (correct)\n\nThe bug is that when there's a single lookup choice without an empty choice option, the filter gets hidden even though it should display. The comparison threshold of `> 1` doesn't account for the always-present \"All\" option, so a single real choice should still show the filter. choices + \"All\"). So the condition should be: `1 + len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 1`, which simplifies to `len(self.lookup_choices) + extra > 0`. But that would show the filter even with just one choice, which seems wrong.\n\nLet me reconsider what makes sense: the filter is only useful if there are actual alternatives to \"All\". So I need at least 2 total options displayed. That means `len(self.lookup_choices) + extra >= 1` would be the right threshold—showing the filter when there's at least one real choice beyond \"All\". (lookup_choices) + 1 > 1 → len(lookup_choices) > 0\n- If not include_empty_choice: len(lookup_choices) > 1\n\nThe bug is clear: when include_empty_choice is True, it only needs 1 lookup choice, but when False, it requires 2. The correct approach should be `len(self.lookup_choices) > 0 or self.include_empty_choice` to show the dropdown if there's at least one choice available or an empty option is included.\n\nLooking at the current implementation more carefully, when include_empty_choice is True and there's 1 lookup choice, it evaluates to 1 + 1 > 1 (True, shows). When False with 1 choice, it's 1 + 0 > 1 (False, hides). But the actual problem reported is that the filter appears even with zero related objects. Testing that scenario: with empty lookup_choices, both cases evaluate to False (0 + 1 > 1 and 0 + 0 > 1), so the widget should hide. Yet the issue persists, suggesting the problem might lie elsewhere in how the condition is being applied or evaluated.\n\nThe base FieldListFilter class unconditionally returns True from has_output(), but RelatedFieldListFilter overrides this at line 248. The filter displays only when there's something meaningful to filter by—the (None) option alone isn't sufficient.
